Predicted Answer: A: Variable expressivity refers to a condition where a single genotype results in variable symptoms or manifestations in different family members. This is consistent with the presentation of this patient's family and his nonaffected status. Maternal uniparental disomy would occur if one member of a dizygotic twin pair inherited all chromosomes from one parent, but this does not apply to the pedigree shown. Gonadal mosaicism occurs when there are two populations of cells within an individual (one normal, one abnormal) and can be seen in individuals who have seemingly sporadic disease, but it is less likely given the pedigree pattern shown. Incomplete penetrance would refer to a condition where one genotype does not result in any symptoms, which does not apply in this case since there are clearly affected family members with that same genotype.

Predicted Answer: A: This patient has features of Pompe disease, a disorder caused by lysosomal acid maltase deficiency. The most common clinical presentation is cardiorespiratory failure in infants. Infants typically present at 6-9 months with symptoms such as poor feeding, regurgitation, and respiratory distress. There are usually findings of cardiomegaly on chest x-ray along with distended neck veins and an S3 gallop heard over the heart. The liver is often palpable, and there may be muscular weakness and proximal muscle masses (also known as "pseudo-Hoffmann–Meigs' sign"). Pompe disease is inherited in an autosomal recessive pattern. Options A, B, and D can all be eliminated because they cause glycogen storage disorders that are associated with hypoglycemia, hepatomegaly, and no significant cardiac findings at birth or in early infancy.

Predicted Answer: A: Tumor necrosis factor-alpha is a cytokine involved in the pathogenesis of septic shock. Neisseria meningitidis infections typically result from bacterial meningitis caused by gram-negative rods. These infections are often characterized by high fevers, confusion, dyspnea, hypotension, petechiae, purpura, and positive Kernig and Brudzinski signs. This patient's symptoms and lab results make Neisseria meningitidis the most likely cause of her bacterial meningitis and septic shock. A: TNF-alpha is a cytokine that plays a key role in systemic inflammation during infections like Neisseria meningitidis, which causes septic shock in this patient. The other options are not associated with the pathogenesis of septic shock caused by gram-negative bacteria such as Neisseria meningitidis. Interleukin-5 is produced primarily by activated CD4+ T cells, mast cells, and basophils. It plays a role in the regulation of IgA production and B cell growth. Interleukin-12 is secreted by macrophages and promotes Th1 response development, which leads to increased cytotoxicity against infected cells. Interleukin-4 is primarily produced by mast cells, basophils, activated T lymphocytes, and NK2 T cells, and plays a role in IgE production and B cell activation. These cytokines do not play a key role in the pathogenesis of septic shock associated with gram-negative bacterial infections such as those caused by Neisseria meningitidis.

Retrieved Content: Arm          Swelling, tenderness clavicle (fracture)
                 Flail arm (brachial plexus injury)                 Swelling, diminished movement (infection, fracture)                 Radial deviation of hand (T AR syndrome)

Predicted Answer: A

Explanation: A fracture of the scaphoid bone is a common injury in patients who fall on an outstretched hand. Symptoms and signs include wrist swelling, tenderness between the extensor pollicis longus and brevis tendons, decreased motion, decreased sensation over the thumb, and a painful radial or dorsal wrist. If left untreated, there can be avascular necrosis of the scaphoid bone with eventual arthritis. A good way to evaluate for this is by doing an x-ray series in 2-3 weeks to see if any fracture fragments are present. Typically, two views of the wrist (anterior-posterior and lateral) will not identify a scaphoid fracture because it is often located just distal and proximal to the midline of the wrist. Therefore, a more detailed view (scaphoid view) is needed, as well as a view from 45 degrees on each side to evaluate for any occult fractures. An MRI may also be used if there is suspicion of scaphoid fracture and an x-ray is negative but clinical suspicion remains high.

 Choice A is correct. Choice B is incorrect because while an MRI could be used in cases where an x-ray is negative, the best first step would be to get a radiograph, as described above. Choice C is incorrect because thumb spica casts are typically used for Skier's thumb (a gamekeeper's thumb) injury, which involves a ligamentous injury of the ulnar collateral ligament at the base of the thumb. A scaphoid fracture should not be treated with a cast and requires imaging studies as described above to confirm or rule out the diagnosis. Choice D is incorrect because while a radial gutter cast may be used for certain wrist fractures, it would not be appropriate for a suspected scaphoid fracture.

Explanation: The symptoms described are most consistent with a vitamin C deficiency, which is composed primarily of glycine amino acids. Vitamin C is necessary for production and maintenance of collagen, the protein that gives skin its strength. Temporal wasting, bruising and bleeding gums, petechiae on the hard palate (or elsewhere), and poor wound healing are all classic symptoms of scurvy, a vitamin C deficiency. This woman's symptoms are likely related to depression, but her physical symptoms are primarily due to defective collagen synthesis (scurvy). Retrieved Content: rate reaches 30%. Among vertically infectedchildren, 5–10% presents an abnormal outcome. This risk ishigher when maternal infection occurs in the first 20 weeksof pregnancy.
Predicted Answer: A: This patient has cystic fibrosis (CF), which is an autosomal recessive disease meaning it is caused by mutations in both copies of a gene on chromosome 7. The genotype for CF patients is typically homozygous recessive (hh) whereas the genotype for those without the disease is heterozygous (Hh). In this question, let H represent the normal allele and h represent the diseased allele. Her parents would have to both be carriers of the disease (genotype: Hh), which means her mother's genotype was either (1) Hh or (2) hh because if she were HH, then there is a 0% chance she could pass on a disease-causing allele to the child (which makes option B incorrect). Since she has CF herself and also had parents, it would mean that one of her parents must have been sick with CF. If either parent is homozygous recessive for cystic fibrosis then there is a 100% chance that they will pass on their disease-causing allele to the child. Therefore, in order for the patient to have CF, each of her parents would have had to be Hh. Her father, however, does not have this disease, so therefore he must have been (1) HH or (2) hh because if either were true, then there is a 0% chance that he could pass on a disease-causing allele to the child. This leaves only one option for her father and that means her father's genotype was (1) Hh. Therefore, his genotype was (Hh). Since both parents are carriers of the diseased gene, each child has a 25% chance of being homozygous recessive (hh), which would cause the disease; therefore there is a 75% chance that they will not have this disease. This means that 1/4 or 25% of their children would have the disease and 3/4 of their children, or 75%, would not, making option A correct.
The best answer is A.
Correct Answer: A

Retrieved Content: cases [10]. The inheritance is autosomal dominant and parentsmust be always investigated for mild clinical signs. Newbornsshow hypertelorism, upslanting palpebral fissures, low-setposteriorly rotated ears, neck pterygium, a shield chest withdeformation of the sternum, and lymphedema
Predicted Answer: A: This condition is known as familial juvenile chronic arthritis (FCJA), which presents similarly in males but milder symptoms in affected females. The disorder is characterized by joint disease that leads to an elevated level of uric acid and eventual kidney failure, often resulting in the premature death of both male cousins. Males inherit only a single X chromosome; therefore, when a son inherits an abnormal X chromosome, he will express the disease because there are no normal genes on his sole X chromosome to compensate for this gene's mutation. A mother would be asymptomatic as her two X chromosomes would contain at least one copy of the mutated gene. Female cousins who inherit only one of their mother's X chromosomes containing the mutation may have symptoms, but usually these symptoms will be milder compared with those experienced by male family members. Therefore, this disorder follows an X-linked recessive pattern. (Choice B) This choice is incorrect because if a mother were to pass on the mutated gene, it would appear in all of her offspring. The disease would not skip generations as observed in this pedigree. (Choice C) This choice is incorrect because inheritance of autosomal dominant genes will be passed on equally between parents and their offspring. (Choice D) Mitochondrial inheritance is a rare mode of transmission that can be inherited only from the mother.

The best answer is A.

Predicted Answer: A) The patient's symptoms of irregular menstrual bleeding, oily skin, severe acne, hirsutism, tall stature, BMI slightly above normal, increased LH, and low FSH levels suggest an androgen excess disorder. Given her age, height, and other laboratory values, the most likely diagnosis is polycystic ovary syndrome (PCOS). Measurement of 17-hydroxyprogesterone (17-OHP) and cortisol can help identify a rare but serious cause of PCOS, congenital adrenal hyperplasia (CAH), which would be characterized by an elevated level of 17-OHP. Elevated levels of 17-OHP can also indicate nonclassic CAH. Because patients with CAH are at risk for developing Cushing syndrome due to increased ACTH production by the pituitary gland, this is the most appropriate next step in screening for comorbidities in this patient. B) A raised level of CA-125 can be found in a variety of conditions that cause ascites or peritoneal irritation but would not directly relate to the symptoms of this patient. C) Blood glucose and cholesterol levels are elevated in some patients with PCOS, as they often have insulin resistance. D) Measurement of TSH (thyroid-stimulating hormone) and T4 (thyroxine) can help determine whether hypothyroidism is a contributing factor to her menstrual irregularities; however, the presence of hirsutism and other clinical findings in this patient make it less likely that she has hypothyroidism.

Retrieved Content: ways by different ventilators and so I will concentrate on theprinciples.
•The lung volume is produced and maintained by a con-tinuous high mean airway pressure ~10–20 cmH
2O, not
just an end expiratory pressure of ~5 cmH2O.
Predicted Answer: D
Explanation: (D)  The conducting airways and upper airway are anatomical dead space, which refers to the volume of gas that does not participate in gas exchange. This includes the upper airway volume (100 mL), conducting airway volume (125 mL), as well as residual volume (RV) (1,000 mL). The RV is the amount of air left behind in the lungs after a maximal expiration and thus does not have an opportunity to participate in gas exchange. Therefore, D is correct. To calculate this answer, you must be able to add these volumes together: 100 + 125 + 1000 = 1,225 mL.

Retrieved Content: 120.7.7 Disorders Presenting with Liver
Failure
Predicted Answer: A) Metformin is an oral antidiabetic agent that works by decreasing glucose production in the liver. However, this mechanism can lead to a rare but serious condition called lactic acidosis, which occurs when metformin inhibits pyruvate dehydrogenase and increases lactate levels in tissues with inadequate oxygenation. This side effect is much more common in patients with heart failure, liver disease, or other conditions that increase the risk of tissue hypoxia. Although not directly causing an elevated liver function test (transaminitis), metformin can contribute to a patient’s elevated liver enzymes through lactic acidosis and subsequent tissue damage. 

The best answer is A.

Retrieved Content: 96.3 Clinical Presentation
NEC presents with signs of gastrointestinal dysfunction suchas bilious gastric residuals, emesis, abdominal distension,hematochezia and/or signs of systemic illness characterized
by apnea and respiratory distress, lethargy, temperature insta-
Predicted Answer: A) The patient's presentation is suggestive of secretory diarrhea due to a systemic disorder. Diarrhea lasting more than 4 weeks in an adult suggests organic disease and should prompt further investigation. A history of recent travel may raise suspicion for enteric infections, but this patient has darkened mucosa with interspersed white spots on colonoscopy. This histopathologic picture is suggestive of celiac disease, especially given the patient's long-standing diarrhea and malabsorption (indicated by weight loss). Celiac disease would also explain her anemia and low serum albumin levels. In contrast, the other options are less likely causes of this presentation: secretory diarrhea is not usually associated with carcinoid tumor or VIPoma. This patient does not have symptoms of a pheochromocytoma (such as hypertension), which makes option D unlikely.
Correct Answer: D
